SUMMARY OF CERTAIN INFORMATION 
RELATING TO THE PAY FOR SUCCESS MODEL 
Environmental Impact Bond Overview 
Environmental Impact Bonds are a form of  debt characterized by a Pay for Success 
component that determines the amount that investors are repaid based on environmental 
performance of the Green Infrastructure project fi nanced by the EIBs.  Investors in EIBs receive 
principal and interest as with a traditional debt issuance.  In addition, an EIB is structured with 
Performance Tiers bounded by key performance be nchmarks or thresholds of a designated 
Outcome Metric which will lead to the payment of a Performance Payment upon the achievement 
of these pre-determined environmental outcomes according to the tiers.  To compensate the issuer 
of the EIB, a concessionary inte rest rate is agreed upon which can reduce overall return to the 
purchasers of the EIB if the pre-determined environmental outcomes are not achieved. 
In connection with the Series 2018D Bonds, two Performance Tiers, a Base Performance 
Outcome and a High Performance Outcome, have been set and a Performance Payment will be 
due and payable to the holders of the Series 2018D Bonds only if the Independent Validator has 
confirmed that a High Performance Outcome has been achieved.  
A portion of the proceeds of the Series 2018D Bonds will finance the Series 2018D Project, 
which currently includes the design and construction of a collection of six bioretention, stream and 
wetland restoration, and Green Infrastructure projects in the Proctor Creek watershed on the West 
Side of the City which are part of the Department's Green Infrastructure program.  The Series 
2018D Project will be concentrated in the ne ighborhoods of English Avenue, Bankhead, Grove 
Park, Hunter Hills, and Mozley Park.  Downstream of and somewhat disconnected from the City 
center, these neighborhoods suffer issues related to  localized flooding and water quality, as well 
as high unemployment, lack of usable greenspa ce, and household incomes of roughly half of the 
City-wide average.  Therefore, while the Department has already proven successful at 
implementing Green Infrastructure projects, the components of the Series 2018D Project were 
developed to address not just the environmen tal issues these neighborhoods suffer, but also 
socioeconomic and public infrastructure concerns.  Each component of the Series 2018D Project 
will be installed in highly visible locations on a combination of right of ways owned by the City, 
City-owned and operated public parks, and unused and overgrown parcels of land being acquired 
by the City.  While different projects will generate different types of environmental, social, 
economic, and health benefits, co mmon to all projects is capture of stormwater, which directly 
mitigates both flooding and water quality challenges.  The components of the Series 2018D Project 
are designed to provide at least 6.4 million gallons of additional stormwater storage capacity in the 
Proctor Creek watershed, resulting in an annual reduction of approximately 56 million gallons in 
stormwater runoff through Green Infrastructure.  See "SUMMARY OF CERTAIN 
INFORMATION RELATING TO THE PAY FOR SUCCESS MODEL - Contingency Plan" 
herein for a discussion of the process by whic h one or more components of the Series 2018D 
Project may be replaced. E-5 
The City and the Performance Payment Agent, on behalf of the holders of the Series 2018D 
Bonds, will enter into the Covenants Agreement in order to execute a Pay for Success model to 
achieve certain environmental outcomes associated with the Series 2018D Project.  Pursuant to the 
Covenants Agreement, a Performance Payment to the holders of the Series 2018D Bonds may be 
made dependent upon the volume capacity of stor mwater capture from the green infrastructure 
interventions occasioned by the Series 2018D Proj ect.  Greater volume capt ure is equivalent to 
greater efficacy of th e Series 2018D Project in terms of flood mitigation and water quality, 
reducing treatment costs to the City as well as damage and disruptions related to flooding.   
Overview of the Department's Green Infrastructure Program 
The City has established a significant need for stormwater management and has committed 
to the use of Green Infrastructure as a key stra tegy for tackling this need.  If not addressed, 
stormwater problems such as localized flooding, deteriorated stormwater infrastructure, and 
impaired creeks, may impede economic development and the quality of life for the citizens of 
Atlanta.  The Department has re solved some of these water quality and flooding issues in part 
through rehabilitation of the Wastewater System.  However, stormwater management has suffered 
from lack of dedicated funding, even as regulatory requirements have increased.  The Department's 
Watershed Management Plan estimates a $25 million annual need for stormwater capital 
improvement projects and operations and maintenance.  As the Department continues to address 
issues related to stormwater runoff under th ese compromised funding circumstances, the 
Department is increasingly looking to supplemen t traditional gray infrastructure systems with 
innovative Green Infrastructure solutions that are more aesthetically appealing, environmentally 
friendly, and cost effective. The Department is turning to Green Infrastructure to address sewer 
capacity relief and has identified Green Infrastructure projects in its Watershed Improvement Plans 
to address water quality.  To cover the impacts of private development and redevelopment, the 
Department now requires the use of Green Infrastructure practices, resulting in millions of gallons 
of stormwater runoff reduction City-wide.  Furthe r, as the member utility for one of six cities on 
the U.S. Water Alliance's Water Equity Taskfo rce, the Department is committed to adopting 
equitable water policies and prac tices that foster community re silience in the face of climate 
change and sees Green Infrastructure as a critical tool to achieve this objective. 
Description of Proctor Creek Watershed 
The Proctor Creek watershed is the only major watershed that is entirely contained within 
the geographic limits of the City.  Proctor Creek is a tributary of the Chattahoochee River and runs 
through the City's west side, a low-income area, with high unemployment, household incomes of 
/g85/g82/g88/g74/g75/g79/g92/g3 /g75/g68/g79/g73/g3 /g82/g73/g3 /g87/g75/g72/g3 /g38/g76/g87/g92/g4136/g90/g76/g71/g72/g3 /g68/g89/g72/g85/g68/g74/g72/g15/g3 /g76/g81/g71/g88/g86/g87/g85/g76/g68/g79/g3 /g69/g85/g82/g90/g81/g73/g76/g72/g79/g71/g86/g3 /g86/g76/g87/g72/g86/g15/g3 /g73/g79/g82/g82/g71/g76/g81/g74/g3 /g68/g81/g71/g3 /g90/g68/g87/g72/g85/g3 /g84/g88/g68/g79/g76/g87/g92/g3
issues, and lack of usable greenspace.  Proctor Creek's headwaters are situated in the highly 
urbanized downtown area, beneath the Georgia World Congress Center and the new Mercedes 
Benz Stadium, where impervious surfaces such as streets, sidewalks, parking lots and rooftops 
prevent rainfall from infiltrating into the soil.   
Goals of the Series 2018D Project 
The City contracted an engineering team led by the CH2MH-Rohadfox Joint Venture 
(CH2M Hill Engineers, Inc. and Rohadfox Cons truction Control Services Corporation), with E-6 
selected subconsultants (Pond & Company, Lowe Engineers) (collectively, the "Engineering 
Consultant"), to design the six current com ponents of the Series 2018D Project, and prepare 
construction cost estimates and procurement documents. 
The primary goals of the Series 2018D Project are to mitigate flooding and improve water 
quality by reducing the impact of stormwater runoff on combined sewer systems and waterways. 
Specific objectives include: (a) reducing the total volume and rate of stormwater runoff discharged 
to the environment; (b) reducing the pollutant load  (nutrients, pathogens, and sediment) of water 
entering area streams; (c) creating and enhancing green space within the City through revegetation 
and removal of impervious surfaces; (d) restoring and improving native habitat for wildlife and 
pollinators; and (e) providing public environmental education.  In addition, the Series 2018D 
Project will have the added a dvantage of providing multiple environmental, economic, and 
community benefits to residents of the City , including partnerships with local workforce 
development organizations to pr ovide access to training and em ployment opportunities in Green 
Infrastructure construction, inspection, and maintenance. 
Outcome Metric 
The calculated volume of stormwater captured or detained by the Series 2018D Project, as 
reflected by the Volume Capture Capacity, was chosen as the decision metric for the calculation 
of environmental benefit because it is: (a) directly related to the primary project outcomes – 
volume storage directly impacts flood reduction and water quality improvements; (b) cost effective 
to quantify – volume can be measured using surveys with reasonable assumptions; (c) objective – 
measurements are taken by registered land surveyors, verified by professionals, and can be 
repeated, if desired; and (d) relevant across all six current components of the Series 2018D Project 
– volume is a relevant metric for stormwat er management practices (English Avenue 
Neighborhood Streets Project, Grove Park Green Infrastructure), stream restoration (Greensferry 
Stream & and Floodplain Restoration Project and Mosquito Hole Stream Restoration Project) and 
constructed wetlands (Va lley of the Hawks Constructed Wetl ands Project), and thus can be 
aggregated into a single performance measure. 
Estimation of Expected Volume 
The expected capacity to capture or retain stormwater volume (in gallons) by each of the 
components of the Series 2018D Project was calculated by the Engineering Consultant according 
to their designs for each component of the Seri es 2018D Project.  Estimates for design purposes 
were made using Computer Aided Design (CAD) drawings compared to surveyed initial 
conditions.  These are routine estimates for engineering companies that are used to calculate 
excavation volumes.  Aggregation of the expected capacity to capture stormwater volume of all 
components of the Series 2018D Project was chosen to simplify the prediction and determination 
of the outcome.  A single aggregated volume also allows for some expected variability in 
individual project volume.  The expected Volume Capture Capacity of the Series 2018D Project, 
as designed, is 6,481,883 gallons while the Hi gh Performance Outcome volume is set as 
6,520,000 gallons.  See "SUMMARY OF CERTAIN INFORMATION RELATING TO THE 
PAY FOR SUCCESS MODEL - Contingency Plan" he rein for a discussion of the process by 
which one or more components of the Series 2018D Project may be replaced. E-7 
Probability Analysis 
In order to determine the anticipated range of the Volume Capture Capacity that can be 
achieved by the Series 2018D Project, a third-pa rty consultant was retained to develop a 
probability model that factors in the primary va riables that could influence Volume Capture 
Capacity (the "Probability Analysis").  Th e final constructed volume capture of Green 
Infrastructure practices may vary from the designe d volume based on a number of factors.  The 
primary factors addressed in the Probability An alysis include project construction bid cost, 
unforeseen subsurface utilities, and contractor performance/field adjustments.   
Contingency Plan 
While the Department will make every effort to complete all six components currently 
comprising the Series 2018D Project, all as more fully described under the caption 
"DESCRIPTION OF THE SERIES 2018D PROJECT" in the Limited Offering Memorandum, 
unforeseen conditions such as those described under "SUMMARY OF CERTAIN 
INFORMATION RELATING TO THE PAY FOR SUCCESS MODEL - Certain Investment 
Considerations" herein may necessitate replacement of one or more components of the Series 
2018D Project.  The Department has developed an alternate strategy should it be unable to continue 
with one or more of the components of the Seri es 2018D Project.  If the Department decides to 
cease work on one of the components of the Series 2018D Project, a new Green Infrastructure 
project or practice will be substituted which will be designed to reach the original intended Volume 
Capture Capacity to the extent reasonably pr acticable until funding is exhausted or nearly 
exhausted.  Replacement projects may include: 
(a) Additional stormwater planters with in the English Avenue Neighborhood; 
locations have been identified. 
(b) Additional stormwater management pr actices, such as bioretention areas or 
pervious pavement, within the tw o Parks projects: Mozley Park and Grove Park.  The City has 
developed conceptual designs for the proposed "add-on" sites.   
(c) Installation of stormwater management practices, such as bioretention areas or 
pervious pavement, in Maddox Pa rk.  A conceptual design for Green Infrastructure in Maddox 
Park has been developed. 
(d) Expansion of the Greensferry project to obtain additional floodplain storage and 
greater volume.   
Notwithstanding the foregoing, the City cannot  guarantee that projects replacing one or 
more components of the Series 2018D Project will  achieve a similar degree  of Volume Capture 
Capacity.  For additional information regarding certain investment  considerations, see 
"SUMMARY OF CERTAIN INFORMATION RELATING TO THE PAY FOR SUCCESS 
MODEL - Certain Investment Considerations" herein. E-8 
Certain Investment Considerations 
The Performance Payment, if and to the extent paid, is contingent upon the effectiveness 
of the Series 2018D Project in producing validated Volume Capture Capacity in the Proctor Creek 
watershed basin indicating a High Performance Outcome prior to the Performance Payment Due 
Date.  Outside of the scope of the Probability Analysis, other unexpected factors may impact 
delivery of the Series 2018D Project, including but not limited to: 
(a) Challenges with Property Acquisition.  The City does not currently own the land 
for two components of the Series 2018D Project:  Valley of the Hawks Constructed Wetland and 
Greensferry Stream Restoration.  The City is presently pursuing acquisition of both sites with the 
assistance of The Conservation Fund ("TCF"), a non-profit land acquisition partner, under a Letter 
of Intent to subsequently acqui re the properties from TCF.  La nd control of both sites via this 
arrangement is anticipated in early 2019.  As of December 31, 2018, TCF is negotiating a contract 
on the Greensferry Stream Restoration site, whic h property is being willingly transferred for the 
purposes of restoration and public use, and the current owner previously executed a Right of Entry 
allowing the City to undertake engineering and su rvey work.  In addition, TCF is in negotiations 
for the three parcels at the Valley of the Hawks Constructed Wetland site and has a verbal 
commitment from the owner for two of the three parc els.  The City will make every good faith 
effort to effectuate the acquisition of the Valley of the Hawks Constructed Wetland and 
Greensferry Stream Restoration sites, however, if unforeseen obstacles jeopardize the acquisition 
of either of the Valley of the Hawks Construc ted Wetland and Greensferry  Stream Restoration 
sites, the City does not intend to construct the related components of the Series 2018D Project.  In 
the event conditions necessitate replacement of one or more of the sites, a new component will be 
substituted, which will be designed to meet the intended Volume Capture Capacity of the Series 
2018D Project to the extent reasonably practicable until funding is exhausted or nearly exhausted. 
(b) Land or Groundwater Contamination.  The Proctor Creek watershed is in or close 
to industrial or formerly industrial areas of the City.  These industries may have released regulated 
chemicals or materials.  Additionally, both illegal and regulated dumping has occurred throughout 
the Proctor Creek watershed.  At this time, site  investigations have not been conducted to 
determine if cleanup is necessary and if so, the expected cost of the cleanup.  The Department has 
included a contingency in the construction budget to account for potential unexpected costs or cost 
overruns.  In the case that remediation needs exc eed the allotted contingency, the Department is 
prepared to contribute Revenues of the System to meet these needs to the extent deemed reasonably 
practicable. 
(c) Unforeseen Weather Events.  Unfores een weather events, such as tornadoes, 
flooding, hurricanes, or extended damaging winter weather, could cause adjustments in the 
components of the Series 2018D Project due to damage to sites or shifting priorities of the City.   
(d) Unforeseen Labor Conditions.  Unforeseen labor conditions, such as strikes or 
labor shortages, could create challenges in co mpleting one or more co mponents of the Series 
2018D Project on schedule and within budget.   
(e) Unforeseen Social Conditions.  Unfores een social conditions, such as riots or 
uprisings, related or unrelated to the Series 2018D Project, could create challenges in completing E-9 
one or more components of Series 2018D Project  on schedule and within budget.  Significant 
criminal activity, such as repeated theft of contractor equipment, could create challenges in 
completing one or more components of the Series 2018D Project on schedule and within budget.   
SUMMARY OF CERTAIN PROVISIONS OF THE COVENANTS AGREEMENT 
The following is a brief summary of certain provisions of the Covenants Agreement, 
including certain provisions of the Technical Memorandum.  This summary is not comprehensive, 
nor is it intended to be a full statement of the terms of such documents and, accordingly, is qualified 
by reference to the Covenants Agreement and the Technical Memorandum, in their entirety, for a 
complete statement of the detailed provisions thereof. 
Simultaneously with the issuan ce of the Series 2018D Bonds, the City will enter into the 
Covenants Agreement, pursuant to which the City will agree to make the Performance Payment to 
the Performance Payment Agent in the event that the Independent Validator validates that the 
Series 2018D Project will produce a Volume Capture Capacity which constitutes a High 
Performance Outcome. 
Project Evaluation  
The Series 2018D Project will be evaluated on the basis of the validated aggregate Volume 
Capture Capacity for purposes of determining if a Performance Payment is due as provided under 
"SUMMARY OF CERTAIN PROVISIONS OF THE COVENANTS 
AGREEMENT - Performance Tiers" herein.  The Volume Capture Capacity will be calculated in 
accordance with the methodology described in the Technical Memorandum and will be verified in 
the Final Validation Report.  See "SUMMARY OF CERTAIN PROVISIONS OF THE 
COVENANTS AGREEMENT - Measurement Methodology" herein. 
Certificate of Completion. The City will provi de the Certificate of Completion to the 
Independent Validator. 
Final Validation Report.  The Independent Validator will issue the Final Validation Report 
to the Performance Payment Agent and the City within 180 days of the date of the Certificate of 
Completion.  The results contained in the Final Validation Report will se rve as the basis for 
determining the projected performance outcomes for the Series 2018D Project, as described under 
"SUMMARY OF CERTAIN PROVISIONS OF THE COVENANTS AGREEMENT - Project 
Evaluation and Performance Tiers - Performance Tiers" herein. 
Contents of Final Validation Report.  The Final Validation Report will indicate whether 
the aggregate Volume Capture Capacity for the Series 2018D Project results in a High 
Performance Outcome, with such evaluatio n being undertaken in compliance with the 
methodology described in the Technical Memorandum, in all material respects.  For a summary of 
the methodology described in the Technical  Memorandum, see "SUMMARY OF CERTAIN 
PROVISIONS OF THE COVENANTS AGREEMENT - Measurement Methodology" herein.  
The obligation to pay the Performance Payment will be conditioned upon receipt of the Final 
Validation Report confirming a High Performan ce Outcome on or before the Performance 
Payment Due Date.  The Independent Validator will deliver the Final Validation Report to the City E-10 
and to the Performance Payment Agent at the same time.  The Final Validation Report will be due 
no later than 180 days after submittal of the Certificate of Completion. 
Performance Tiers  
The effectiveness of the Series 2018D Project will be determined by the City based upon 
the results contained in the Final Validation Re port as corresponding to one of two Performance 
Tiers. 
(a) a High Performance Outcome; or 
(b) a Base Performance Outcome. 
Measurement Methodology 
In accordance with the Technical Memorandum , to evaluate perform ance the Contractor 
will measure final volume captured per Green Infrastructure practice and deliver as-built drawings 
certifying the measurements to the Department following final completion of each component of 
the Series 2018D Project, according to the terms of the related construction contract(s).  Pursuant 
to the Technical Memorandum, because "Volume Capture" will be measured as a capacity, not a 
flow, this will be a one-time measurement that will determine the Performance Tier and whether 
the Performance Payment is due and payable.  Per-practice volumes will be aggregated into a 
single outcome metric to be re ported to the holders of the Series 2018D Bonds at the end of the 
Project Verification Period. 
Performance Payment 
The Performance Payment Agent will provide written notice to the Bond Registrar and 
Paying Agent, on or before the Performance Payment Due Date as to whether a Performance 
Payment is due under the Covenants Agreement, as follows: 
(a) If a Final Report is received, prior to the Performance Payment Due Date, which 
indicates a High Performance Outcome the Performance Payment Agent shall provide written 
notification to the City that the holders of Series 2018D Bonds are due the Performance Payment. 
(b) If either no Final Report is received pr ior to the Performance Payment Due Date or 
a Final Report is received which does not indicate a High Performance Outcome, the Performance 
Payment Agent shall provide written notification to the City that no Performance Payment is due. 
(c) If due as provided under (i) above, the amount of the Performance Payment will be 
$1,000,000. 
Any Performance Payment, if paid, shall not co nstitute or be treated as principal of or 
interest on the Series 2018D Bonds for any purpo se of the Bond Ordinance, including, without 
limitation, the Debt Service Requirement and the Rate Cove nant set forth in the Bond Ordinance 
or any conditions for the issuance of Bonds or  Subordinate Bonds.  A Performance Payment will 
not constitute Senior Bonds or  Subordinate Bonds under the B ond Ordinance.  A Performance 
Payment will be secured by a promise to pay from Net Operating Revenues that is subordinate to 
the pledge of Net Operating Revenues that secures Senior Bonds and Subordinate Bonds. E-11 
Verification 
In accordance with the Technical Memora ndum, the Independent Validator has been 
retained to provide third-part y evaluation and verification of environmental performance of the 
Series 2018D Project relative to the Outcome Metric and will verify the accuracy of each 
contractor's as-built survey results via site visits  and review of submittals.  The fees and costs of 
the Independent Validator are included in the budget for the Series 2018D Project. 
The verification process will consist of the following three stages which will culminate in 
the determination of whether a High Performance Outcome is achieved and, if so, the payment of 
the Performance Payment on the Performance Payment Date: 
(a) Construction Period Monitoring, which is  expected to occur between months one 
through 36 (three years), or no later than 60 months (five years); 
(b) Project Verification, exp ected to occur between months 24 through 48 (years two 
through four), or no later than 66 months, concurrent with and following the construction period; 
and 
(c) Final Validation Report, expected to be prepared in years three through four, but 
no later than year six. 
Reporting 
The City will provide to the Performance Payment Agent reports on the status of the Series 
2018D Project beginning with the third full month after the City has issued a Notice to Proceed 
for construction of any portion of the Series 2018D Project, and quarterly thereafter on each 
January 1, April 1, June 1 and September 1 until the issuance of the Certificate of Completion, the 
City will provide quarterly construction progress reports to the Performance Payment Agent.  In 
no event will the City's failure to timely provide an y such reports be deemed an Event of Default 
(as defined herein) with respect to the Series 2018D Bonds or affect the payment of a Performance 
Payment. 
Duties of Performance Payment Agent 
The Performance Payment Agent's sole responsibility will be for the safekeeping and 
disbursement of the funds, including the Escrow  Fund held by the Performance Payment Agent 
under the Covenants Agreement (the  "Custodial Funds") in accordance with the terms of the 
Covenants Agreement.  The Performance Payment Agent will acknowledge and agree that it will 
have no right of set-off arising out of any claims that it may have against the City under any other 
agreement and, as such, agrees to apply the moneys in the Escrow Fund only as provided in the 
Covenants Agreement. 
In the absence of bad faith on its part, th e Performance Payment Agent may conclusively 
rely, as to the truth of the statements and th e correctness of the opinions expressed therein, upon 
certificates furnished to the Performance Payment Agent. 
The Performance Payment Agent will maintain records of all disbursements of 
Performance Payments and any disbursements from the Escrow Fund through the date ending six E-12 
years following the date on which the Series 201 8D Bonds have been retired.  The Performance 
Payment Agent will make such records available upon request to the City and the holders from 
time to time of the Series 2018D Bonds. 
Events or Default and Remedies 
Pursuant to the Covenants Agreement, the following will each constitute an "Event of 
Default" by the City or the Performance Payment Agent, as applicable:   
(a) any material breach by it of any representation made in the Covenants Agreement, 
or  
(b) any material failure by it to observe and perform any covenant, condition or 
agreement on its part to be observed or performed under the Covenants Agreement, in either case 
for a period of 30 days after written notice specifying such breach or failure and requesting that it 
be remedied, given to it by the other party or a beneficiary of the Covenants Agreement; provided 
that in the event such breach or failure can be corrected but cannot be corrected within said 30 day 
period, the same will not constitute a default under the Covenants Agreement if corrective action 
is instituted by or on behalf of the defaulting party within said 30 day period and is being diligently 
pursued, no such extension shall be for a period in excess of 60 days. 
Upon the occurrence and continuance of an  Event of Default under the Covenants 
Agreement by the City or the Performance Payment Agent, as the case may be, the non-defaulting 
party or a beneficiary of the Covenants Agreement may seek specific performance of the 
Covenants Agreement and/or pursue any other remedies available at law or in equity. CITY OF ATLANTA (GEORGIA) • WATER AND WASTEWATER ENVIRONMENTAL IMPACT SUBORDINATE LIEN REVENUE BONDS (PROCTOR CREEK WATERSHED PROJECT), SERIES 2018D
